Feb-17-2017 005275
Subject:        
Regional haze
Clayton, hi, haven’t talked for a while, hope all is well, other than that horrible 10th Cir decision.
I don’t know if you know, but we represent Arizona in its similar appeal of EPA’s regional haze
decision as to Arizona. 
I saw today that AG Pruitt has announced that you will file a petition for
rehearing en banc. 
I’m really glad you decided to do so.
I’m attaching the brief we filed in the Ninth Circuit. 
It was submitted about a week after the OK
decision came down, so we addressed the decision in our brief. 
You will see we spent a great deal of
time on standard of review, because we felt that is the key issue in the case – and where the 10thCircuit really got it wrong because I think its decision conflicts with the Supreme Court’s decision in
Alaska DEC v. EPA. 
It could be a fruitful argument to make in the rehearing petition. 
In fact, I have recommended to the AZ AG’s office that they file an amicus brief in support of yourrehearing request in which they would make this argument, and maybe join with a couple of other
states in doing so. 
Hopefully, we can make that happen.
Good luck.

 Comments.docx
All: 
               
 
The
 
attached
 
document
 
reflects
 
the
 
most
 
recent
 
round
 
of
 
revisions
 
to
 
the
 
proposed
 
rules
for
 
Chapter
 
35. 
 
The
 
revisions
 
were
 
made
 
after
 
Staff’s
 
review
 
and
 
consideration
 
of
 
all
 
interim
comments
 
received
 
December
 
18-19,
 
2013.
 
  The
 
second
 
technical
 
conference
 
for
 
Chapter
 
35
 
will
 
be
held
 
on
 
Tuesday,
 
January
 
14,
 
2014
 
at
 
10:00
 
in

301.

number
 
will
 
be
 
provided
 
soon.

 1.
Wetlands
 
gains/losses
 
metric
 
–
 
The
 
UWA
 
includes
 
a
 
metric
 
that
 
scores
 
watersheds
 
based
 
on
wetlands
 
loss
 
estimates. 
 
The
 
current
 
source
 
of
 
data
 
(USDA
 
NRI
 
study)
 
renders
 
probabilistic
based
 
estimates
 
for
 
HUC
 
8
 
watersheds,
 
but
 
over
 
half
 
of
 
the
 
watersheds
 
show
 
margins
 
of
error
 
that
 
far
 
exceed
 
the
 
estimate
 
itself. 
 
Are
 
there
 
other
 
sources/ideas
 
to
 
represent
 
wetland
gains/losses
 
in
 
the
 
scoring
 
regime?
2.
Conservation
 
Programs
 
metric
 
–
 
The
 
WG
 
voted
 
to
 
amend
 
the
 
“NRCS
 
LEA”
 
metric
 
to
 
include
other
 
conservation
 
related
 
programs
 
(e.g.,
 
CRP,
 
WRP)
 
in
 
addition
 
to
 
source
 
water
 
and
 
well
head
 
protection
 
areas.
 
 A
 
quick
 
application
 
of
 
this
 
appears
 
to
 
show
 
a
 
bolstering
 
of
 
scores
 
for
most
 
watersheds
 
with
 
somewhat
 
limited
 
separation. 
 
We
 
are
 
proposing
 
to
 
potentially
incorporate
 
an
 
element
 
of
 
actual
 
areal
 
percentage
 
of
 
these
 
programs
 
by
 
watershed
 
in
 
place
of
 
or
 
in
 
addition
 
to
 
the
 
current
 
presence/absence
 
scheme. 
 
Issues
 
or
 
comments?
3.
Stream
 
equivalence
 
for
 
lakes
 
–
 
The
 
WG
 
voted
 
to
 
amend
 
the
 
manner
 
by
 
which
 
stream
equivalence
 
was
 
rendered
 
for
 
lakes
 
from
 
the
 
simple
 
areal
 
multiplication
 
method
 
to
 
the
actual
 
NHD
 
hi-res
 
stream
 
network
 
underlying
 
the
 
lake
 
footprint. 
 
This
 
appears
 
to
 
be
rendering
 
a
 
much
 
more
 
realistic
 
stream
 
equivalence. 
 
However,
 
due
 
to
 
the
 
more
 
refined
spatial
 
focus
 
of
 
HUC
 
12s,
 
this
 
means
 
that
 
watersheds
 
with
 
impaired
 
lakes
 
may
 
still
 
receive
the
 
maximum
 
score
 
since
 
most
 
of
 
the
 
watershed
 
will
 
be
 
impaired. 
 
We
 
still
 
have
 
more
 
work
to
 
do
 
to
 
verify
 
this,
 
but
 
please
 
consider
 
possible
 
ways
 
by
 
which
 
we
 
can
 
more
 
equitably
 
and
reasonably
 
represent
 
watersheds
 
with
 
lakes.

Subject:2013 NPS Annual Report Info RequestDate:01/02/2014 01:39 PMAttachments:
OCC 2012 Annual Report.pdf
Happy New Year!
The Oklahoma Conservation Commission is compiling the Oklahoma Nonpoint Source (NPS) Management Program
Annual Report for FY 2013.
 Oklahoma’s NPS management efforts involve many partners in state, federal, and tribal
programs, and it is our desire to reflect significant accomplishments over the past year.
Please submit a brief
 summary of your agency's FY13 NPS management activities
for inclusion in this report.
 You
could even just send a bulleted list.
 Inclusions should focus on
significant accomplishments, quantifiable water quality
improvements, and future actions
planned with regard to nonpoint source issues.
 In addition, please include
goals/milestones of your NPS project, partners in the project, and funding amounts/sources.  
Pictures
are
highly
valued
and
encouraged! 
Reporting period:
 FY 2013 (Oct 1, 2012 to Sept. 30, 2013)
Submittal Deadline:
January 17
th, 2014
About
the NPS Program Annual Report
·
EPA and the State use
the report
to determine the State's progress in implementing the NPS Program.
·
The report is to be an easy-to-read, short reference to the status of the State's efforts to address NPSimpairments.·
The report is written for the EPA, State, and public audiences.·
The NPS Annual Report reaches beyond those efforts and actions funded with 319(h) and reports on allprogram mechanisms outlined in the State's NPS Management Program.
I have attached last year’s report for easy viewing, if you would like to see the type of info that we need.
To view previous years’ reports, please visit our website:
http://www.ok.gov/conservation/Agency_Divisions/Water_Quality_Division/WQ_Reports/WQ_Reports_Annual_Reports/
If any facet of your program has addressed NPS issues this year, please send the pertinent information toStacey Day at 
stacey.day@conservation.ok.gov
Thanks for your help!
 ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~Stacey DaySr. Technical WriterOklahoma Conservation Commission, Water Quality Division4545 N. Lincoln Blvd., Suite 11A
Oklahoma City, OK
 73105
(405) 522-4735

Please find attached to this email the Chapter 45 proposed rules that were revised as a result of the
interim comments received by the Public Utility Division on December 18-19, 2013.
 The next
technical conference for the Chapter 45 proposed rules will be held on January 14, 2014, at 1:30p.m. in courtroom 301.
Thank you.
(I apologize if you have received this e-mail twice).

Subject:Chapter 35 Electric Utility Rulemaking - Interim Comment RevisionsDate:01/08/2014 04:33 PMAttachments:
Chapter 35 - Revisions - Condensed
 Comments.docx
All: 
               
 
The
 
attached
 
document
 
reflects
 
the
 
most
 
recent
 
round
 
of
 
revisions
 
to
 
the
 
proposed
 
rules
for
 
Chapter
 
35. 
 
The
 
revisions
 
were
 
made
 
after
 
Staff’s
 
review
 
and
 
consideration
 
of
 
all
 
interim
comments
 
received
 
December
 
18-19,
 
2013.
 
  The
 
second
 
technical
 
conference
 
for
 
Chapter
 
35
 
will
 
be
held
 
on
 
Tuesday,
 
January
 
14,
 
2014
 
at
 
10:00
 
in
 
Room
 
301. 
 
A
 
call-in
 
number
 
will
 
be
 
provided
 
soon.

Subject:Dec. 10th NPS Work Group Meeting Reminder!Date:12/09/2013 02:59 PMI hope you have all survived the winter weather we’ve been having! I wanted to remind you aboutour NPS Working Group webinar tomorrow Tues. Dec. 10, 2013. Hopefully you got the meetingnotice last week with a few questions we had regarding the re-ranking of waterbodies. As mentionedwe have discovered a few things as we began pulling information together that we would like yourinput on. I have included them here again for your convenience. Below is the call in and website linkfor you to join the conversation. Please don’t hesitate to contact me with any questions, and asalways you are welcome to join us in our offices at 4545 N. Lincoln Blvd. Ste 11 if you want toparticipate in person.
Jeri Fleming
1.
Wetlands gains/losses metric – The UWA includes a metric that scores watersheds based on
wetlands loss estimates.
 The current source of data (USDA NRI study) renders probabilistic
based estimates for HUC 8 watersheds, but over half of the watersheds show margins of
error that far exceed the estimate itself.
 Are there other sources/ideas to represent wetland
gains/losses in the scoring regime?2.
Conservation Programs metric – The WG voted to amend the “NRCS LEA” metric to includeother conservation related programs (e.g., CRP, WRP) in addition to source water and well
head protection areas. 
A quick application of this appears to show a bolstering of scores for
most watersheds with somewhat limited separation.
 We are proposing to potentially
incorporate an element of actual areal percentage of these programs by watershed in place
of or in addition to the current presence/absence scheme.
 Issues or comments?
3.
Stream equivalence for lakes – The WG voted to amend the manner by which streamequivalence was rendered for lakes from the simple areal multiplication method to the
actual NHD hi-res stream network underlying the lake footprint.
 This appears to be
rendering a much more realistic stream equivalence.
 However, due to the more refined
spatial focus of HUC 12s, this means that watersheds with impaired lakes may still receive
the maximum score since most of the watershed will be impaired.
 We still have more work
to do to verify this, but please consider possible ways by which we can more equitably and
Feb-17-2017 005727
reasonably represent watersheds with lakes.
Call in information for the webinar is as follows:
Jeri Fleming has invited you to a conference call: NPS Management PlanWorking Group Meeting.This conference is scheduled to begin on December 10, 2013 at 09:00 AMCST+ DST (Central).
This conference is scheduled to last for 120 minutes.To access this conference via telephone, please call 405-521-4496,Oklahoma City, OK.When prompted for your conference code, please enter 618163 on yourtelephone keypad.To access the data portion of this conference, please visit the following URLand then follow the instructions:
http://meetingexchange.ok.gov/Conferencing?
BrandPrefix=AVAYA&ConfRef=132890&Pin=618163
As always feel free to contact me with any questions.
Jeri FlemingOklahoma Conservation Commission117 Life Sciences EastStillwater, OK 74078405-334-6343
jeri.fleming@conservation.ok.gov
